Callback props replace event dispatchers for custom events.\n\n## Internationalization\n\nTranslatable strings use hierarchical naming (`server.email.magic_link.subject`) and GNU gettext `.po` files. Built-in defaults (precedence 10)\n2. System config at `/etc/loom/config.toml` (20)\n3. User config via XDG (30)\n4. Workspace-local config (40)\n5. Environment variables prefixed with `LOOM_` (50)\n6. CLI arguments (60)\n\n## Key Features\n\n**XDG Compliance**: Configuration follows the XDG Base Directory Specification, storing files in standardized locations like `~/.config/loom/` and `~/.local/share/loom/` with environment variable overrides available.\n\n**Intelligent Merging**: The system performs deep merging for configuration tables while completely replacing scalar values and arrays based on precedence, allowing flexible overrides at each layer.\n\n**Type Safety**: All configuration undergoes strict validation with comprehensive error messages. The specification includes field-level constraints (e.g., timeout values between 1-3600 seconds) and cross-field validations ensuring referential integrity.\n\n**Auto-Configuration**: When Loom launches without existing user configuration, it automatically generates a default template file with documented options, eliminating zero-configuration friction.\n\n## Provider Support\n\nThe configuration explicitly supports multiple LLM providers: Anthropic, OpenAI, Ollama, and custom OpenAI-compatible services. As specified, \"Secrets are wrapped in a type that enforces redaction at compile time.\"\n\n**Memory Safety**: Secrets are zeroized from memory on drop using the `zeroize` crate, clearing sensitive data when the object is destroyed.\n\n**Explicit Access**: Developers must call `.expose()` to access underlying values, making secret usage visible during code review.\n\n**Logging Integration**: The Debug and Display implementations always return `[REDACTED]` rather than actual values, integrating seamlessly with `tracing` and JSON logging frameworks.\n\n## Architecture\n\nThe system spans three crates:\n- **loom-secret**: Core `Secret<T>` type with no business logic\n- **loom-common-config**: Adds environment loading via `load_secret_env()`\n- **Domain crates**: Implement configuration-specific logic\n\n## File-Based Loading\n\nSupports Docker/Kubernetes conventions where `{VAR}_FILE` takes precedence over `{VAR}`, allowing secrets to be mounted as files rather than stored in environment variables—a production security best practice.\n\n## Testing & Security\n\nProperty-based tests verify secrets never leak through serialization or debug output. The specification distinguishes two authentication modes:\n\n1. **API Key mode**: Single static key with unlimited quota\n2. **OAuth Pool mode**: Multiple Pro/Max subscriptions with failover capabilities\n\n## Core Components\n\n**Account Management:**\n- Each account tracks three states: Available, CoolingDown, or Disabled\n- When an account hits the 5-hour rolling limit, it enters a cooldown period (default 2 hours)\n- The system uses round-robin selection to distribute requests across available accounts\n\n**Error Classification:**\nThe implementation distinguishes three error categories:\n\n- \"Transient\" errors (429 general rate limits, 408, 5xx) trigger retry logic\n- \"QuotaExceeded\" errors (429 with \"5-hour\" or \"rolling window\" in message) trigger failover\n- \"Permanent\" errors (401, 403) disable the account\n\n## Configuration\n\nEnvironment variables control the setup:\n- `LOOM_SERVER_ANTHROPIC_OAUTH_PROVIDERS`: comma-separated account IDs\n- `LOOM_SERVER_ANTHROPIC_OAUTH_CREDENTIAL_FILE`: path to credentials JSON\n- `LOOM_SERVER_ANTHROPIC_POOL_COOLDOWN_SECS`: cooldown duration\n\n## Health Reporting\n\nThe pool exposes status information showing accounts available, cooling down, or disabled—enabling both monitoring and graceful degradation when capacity is reduced."}]},"uuid":"36d784ef-0cc2-4f37-bc7a-a7b4345a1089","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:39:25.724Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5e1904e2-4cac-4b69-bbf5-fcc3526e06d7","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

The eBPF programs operate in kernel space with minimal overhead, while a Rust userspace component handles event batching, filtering, local buffering, and HTTP delivery.\n\n## Coverage Areas\n\nThe specification addresses 6 major syscall categories:\n\n1. **Process events**: exec, fork, exit\n2. **File operations**: reads, writes, metadata changes\n3. **Network activity**: sockets, connections, DNS queries\n4. **Privilege changes**: uid/gid/capability modifications\n5. **Memory operations**: executable memory mapping\n6. **Sandbox escapes**: namespace/mount/BPF syscalls\n\n## Notable Design Choices\n\n- Events batch every 100ms before transmission\n- Local 256 MB buffer for server downtime resilience\n- Connection state tracking correlates related socket operations\n- DNS responses are cached (TTL-aware, max 10,000 entries) to enrich network events with hostnames\n- Userspace filtering removes low-signal events like standard library reads\n\nThe implementation spans three Rust crates with shared types for eBPF/userspace compatibility."}]},"uuid":"c349845b-aacf-47f7-a90d-01415d24d2b3","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:39:37.590Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"ba052e01-056f-4f84-996a-f8e38811badf","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

Users initiate a browser-based flow where they authorize access, receive an authorization code, and exchange it for short-lived access tokens plus refresh tokens.\n\nThe implementation requires:\n- **Client ID**: A public identifier provided by Anthropic\n- **PKCE**: Mandatory cryptographic verification to prevent code interception\n- **Token refresh**: Automatic mechanism to obtain new access tokens before expiration\n- **Headers**: `Authorization: Bearer <token>` plus required beta flags\n\n## API Key Authentication\n\nPay-per-use access uses static API keys (formatted as `sk-ant-...`). This approach eliminates the need for OAuth flows and token management.
